### Page 6
January 10, 1961 (Enroute to Washington) I visited Thomas Scarpa, president of
International Ultrasonic Corp., Cranford, N.J. yesterday and discussed my soon
to issue patent for Ultrasonic Apparatus with him yesterday. Additional designs,
modifications and applications for this ducted transducer were suggested by me
to him as follows – (a) Use of the ducted ultrasonic transducer of constant
outside diameter shown in my patent application - Ultrasonic Apparatus for (1)
Cleaning or unblocking clogged pipes by directing it therein on the end of a
flexible conduit and operating the transducer per se. I also suggested, and will
file an application on a transducer arrangement with the end of the duct
surrounding the transducer being servo driven to tilt, rotate or angulate while
in the pipe to (a) assist in the unblocking action (b) clean the wall of the
pipe, (c) inspect the inside of the pipe. I also conceive of combining a small
television camera adjacent the transducer or with any electrical or mechanical
(rooter) to visually see what is going on during or before or after the
unblocking action. (2) Mentioned to Scarpa was the possibility of using my
ducted tool as a probe to place into a liquid for chemical reactions (a drawing
Figs. 1 to 5 was left with him) THIS CONFIDENTIAL MATTER READ AND UNDERSTOOD by
Ernest Waldmeyer DATE 1/14/61

1/23/61 MW Read 1/25/61

### Page 7
Jan 10, 1961 (3) Also mentioned was my embodiment in which the duct ~~ ed ~~
housing the transducer is provided with a fluid circulating system which
includes means for removing eroded material, filter, fluid circulating system
etc. Other variations conceived by me which are or will become the subject of
patent applications are as follows (4) Provision for positional adjustment of
transducer in housing of my embodiment in Figs 1 and 2. Adjustment of
transducer(s) towards and away from the orifice. (5) Provision ~~ for ~~ of an
inlet to the housing adjacent the orifice thru which ultrasonic energy is
directed for (a) a blast of a stream of high velocity liquid, gas or ~~ ste ~~
vapor such as steam to be admitted during, prior to or after ultrasonic
transducing to assist in the eroding or cleaning action. Jet or blast to be
directed thru openings in ~~ housing ~~ housing against ~~ to ~~ work surface
which housing abuts and/or directed against part of housing to assist in removal
of particles, dirt, etc removed from work surface. (6) Admission (to housing
surrounding transducer) of material such as abrasive particles etc. which will
aid in eroding. THIS CONFIDENTIAL MATTER READ AND UNDERSTOOD BY EJW DATE 1/14/61

ultrasonically such articles as (disclosed to Scarpa) (a)spark plugs (on the
engine block or removed), which adaptor heads include shaped rubber nose
portions to circumscribe the part, (b) to fit over nuts, bolts, etc. to remove
rust, seizing, calking, etc (8)Provision of an end adapter for my ducted tool

an irregular or expanding shape; and transducer which may be automatically
operated after admission of liquid ~~ to ~~ resulting closed chamber to move
about and scan surface of work as it operates thereon. (9) Also discussed with
Thomas Scarpa was my idea for designing my ultrasonic tool in the shape of a
pistol grip or gun the trigger of which would be coupled to a switch for
energizing the transducer and/or simultaneously admitting a liquid to the
chamber surrounding the transducer. A particular control arrangement would be
one in which a single trigger or switch JL Jan 10, 1961 THIS CONFIDENTIAL MATTER

actuation would result in the simultaneous actuation of the transducer and

predetermined quantity of liquid or continuous flow thereof out the chamber or
circulated therein while nose is in sealing engagement with the work). When the
switch or trigger is released or opened, the transducer energy input is cut off
and either the liquid flow (valve) is closed or the action includes removal of
all liquid from the chamber. JL Jan 10, 1961 I have been working on patent

MW Jan 23, 1961 Car Washing Machine The following system and apparatus is
conceived for cleaning the body of automobiles. (1) Convey auto first thru ~~a
~~ sprays of ~~deter ~~ a strong detergeant (2) Next convey past sprays of water
removing detergent and dirt (3) Then convey past ~~a ~~ sprays of surface
tension lowering chemical or wetting agent (4)Then move auto past a plurality of
hot air nozzles or blowers to roll water off car without streaking. It is also
conceived to polish a surface such as a vehicle body by adding wax in solution
or suspension to the final spray of water and including soft plastic (vinyl)
balls 1/8 to 1/4" diameter to the stream or blast of water to effect THIS
CONFIDENTIAL MATTER READ & UNDERSTOOD BY EJW 1/24/61 JB 1/25/61

### Page 15
polishing and to help secure the wax to the surface ~~of ~~being cleaned. Note:
In car washing process on Page 10, certain of the first sprays may include fine
sprays of a wetting agent. J. Lemelson Jan 23, 1961 Ernest J. Waldmeyer 1/24/61

SYSTEM I talked to Henry Stehling last nite who mentioned the current problem of
entering billing information into computers over telephone lines. Typical
current problems the correction of bills, premiums, additions where there are
many accounts serviced by different representatives, salesmen, delivery men who
report to local offices which information must be transmitted via phone lines to
district offices containing businesses machines and/or computers. Fuel billing
in which a fuel truck driver delivers different quantities of gasoline to
different THIS CONFIDENTIAL MATTER READ & UNDERSTOOD BY MM DATE 2/8/61

### Page 17
31b not 31-b dealers, distributers, etc. Texaco for example delivers bulk fuel
to 1600 stations periodically which is then distributed to thousands of service
stations. In insurance billing, the larger companies require information
scanning of 9 digit alpha-numeric information to account for policy number,
amount billed, variation, amt. paid, etc A number of systems have been conceived
viz. System #I (brief description) This system employs a form, 12 preferably the
size of the bill or receipt (7 1/2" x 8 1/2") which the driver leaves with each
customer upon delivery. The form is preferably stiff paper or card stock. If
simple information such as gallons delivered per trip is ~~ des ~~ the variable
to be recorded at least 25 and possibly 30 entries may be made on one card by
the person making the delivery or a clerk after delivery. The form, as
conceived, utilizes a binary code (although when a character reader is perfected
of higher efficiency than presently available, ~~ a char ~~ written or printed
numbers may be entered on the proper space on the card. Fig. 1 illustrates a
composite record form 10 consisting of plural JL 2/1/61

areas. The strip area 12-1 is divided into two rows Upper row 12-1a is intended
for printed entry of the customer ~~ names ~~ name and/or address. This area,
12-1a, is divided into boxes so that if a character reader is employed or
provided in the future it may scan 12-1a for direct conversion of the
alpha-numeric characters thereof to code or for their identification. Lower row
12-1b contains smaller boxes for entry of a binary bit code. Both rows 12-1a and
12-1b may be printed with an automatic printing machine or may be filled in by
manual means by the person making the delivery. The area designated 12-2 has
alphanumeric printed or written characters and/or binary bit codes representing
the address and other pertinent information on the customer or product
represented by the card 12. The central portion 12-3 of the card 12 JL 2/1/61

opening 21 is provided in side JL 2/1/61 THIS CONFIDENTIAL MATTER READ &

### Page 26
wall 20-2 thru ~~ which ~~ in the card 12 is first placed. A receiving tray 22
is secured to wall 20-2 and projects outward therefrom with the upper surface of
22 being in alignment with the bottom of the slotted opening 21. A side guide 23
defines one end of 22 against which an edge of the card 12 is placed when
placing said card thru the opening 21 for alignment with reading means situated
within 20'. During the reading function, the card 12 is driven in two
directions, first a predetermined distance into the housing as directionally
defined by arrow *A* and then in a direction normal thereto in the direction
defined by arrow *A'.* The degree of movement into the housing in the direction
of "A" is sufficient to center the row or rows of binary (or numerical)
recordings to be read by fixed transducers 31 when the card is driven normal
thereto in direction A' to produce a binary serial code on output 31W. which, as
stated, may extend to a computer, recorder, transmitter, etc. A first drive
means for the card comprises a plurality of elongated rolls which functionally
engage and  the card after it has entered the housing until the card is
prepositioned within the housing after which certain of the rolls retract
automatically after other rolls engage the card for moving it laterally thru the
housing and out an opening 21' in end-wall 20-4 during which lateral movement
reproduction transducing or scanning is effected. JL 2/1/61 THIS CONFIDENTIAL

The first drive means comprises a plurality of bottom rollers 26 which are free
wheeling and are supported on their shafts in bearing by journals 26B which are
secured to a partition 20-7 which extends between the side-walls of the housing.
A plurality of upper rollers 27 are power operated by a motor 30 to drive the
card into the housing when engaged against its upper surface. The rollers ~~ and
m ~~ are bearingly supported on a U-frame 28 by means of a push-pull  29 secured
to top wall 20-5, from a retracted position where the rollers 27 are disengaged
from the card to a projected position engaging the rollers against the card for
driving it into the housing. A  switch 25 having a pivoting activator arm which
is moved by the card upon entering the slot or shortly thereafter ~~ used to
energize the solenoid 29 projecting the upper rollers 27 to engage the card. The
switch 25 is also connected to start motor 30 which drives one or more of the
upper rollers thru gears 30-6 coupled to the shafts of the motors and rollers. A
first pick-up transducer 31' (X) is positioned to read the indicating
recording(s) or mark(s) provided on column 12-10. If a single mark is used to
indicate the position of the row requiring reading then the first pulse
generated on the output of 31 may be  used to ev ~~ passed over the output 31'-W

described by describing a cycle of operation. Limit switch 25 is actuated when
the card enters the slot in the housing 20 and pulses or energizes the start
control 30F of motor 30 and the  projection  advance input 29F of solenoid 29.

or mark in column 12-10 which produces a pulse on the outputof the amplifier 31A
in the circuit of 31'. The pulse is passed to the stop control 30S of motor 30,
retract control 29R of 29,  projectio advance control input 36F of motor 35
Which then causes the card to be driven in the direction of A' with the pick-up
31 aligned with the row 12b to be read. Shown in Fig. 7 is a recording member 48
such as a paper or magnetic tape or recording film on a channel of which the
pulse train generated on the output of 31 is to be recorded. A recording

Feb 13-1961 I spoke to Jim Du Pont by phone of Thermoplastic Processes,
Sterling, N.J. today and briefly described my patent ~~ entit ~~ application
entitled Extrusion Apparatus after inquiring if he would be interested in
investing in its development on a joint venture basis. I had previously written
him asking for a confidential relation which his partner replied to ~~  ~~ and
suggested I come in to see him. J. Lemelson Ultrasonic Devices Feb. 13, 1960 The
following signalling systems using ultrasonic ~~ singa ~~ (sound) signals have
been conceived. I. Paging or remote control system: (a) A relay transducer is
provided which becomes energized upon receipt of a sound signal of a specific
frequency or narrow frequency range. An ultrasonically vibratable transducer
provides an output signal which is amplified and used to energize a switch to
either open or close a circuit upon receipt of said signal. This may be used to
energize a ~~ relay ~~ servo, sound a buzzer, turn on a light, etc (b) The

Devices and Systems The following ultrasonic inventions have been conceived by
me. (1) Ultrasonic cleaning of clothes and other fabric materials. It is
conceived to generate supersonic waves in a chamber into which is introduced a
vapor of cleaning agent on a spray thereof in which the vapor, and/or spray and
the mechanical agitation thereof as well as the article the cleaned results in a
cleaning action. The article may be first immersed, agitated, tumbled, etc. in a
cleaning liquid and thereafter either hung or tumbled in the ~~ ultrasonic ~~
chamber in the presence of said supersonic waves which are also effective in
drying the article. {2) Utilizing ultrasonic vibrations generated in a plastic
material tube in a molten or semi-molten state to (a) increase or speed up
polymerization, (b) improve the physical and chemical characteristics of the
plastic. The ultrasonic transducer may be placed for example in the extrusion
throat of an extruder, upstream of the throat downstream or in the extrusion
die. For processes such as the spinnerette THIS CONFIDENTIAL MATTER READ &
UNDERSTOOD BY BJM JB DATE 2/23/6 EC 3/1/61 LW 3/2/61

exudes therefrom. (3) In dying certain fibers, yarns or cloth such as
polypropylene materials, ultrasonic vibration applied in the dying liquid to the
surface of the yarn, fiber, or cloth may be used to improve the penetration of
the dye into the yarn or fiber (4) In the penetration of matted textiles from

3/22/61 MW 3/20/61 LW

### Page 111

Step 1 - A potential difference V is applied across the series R-C circuit
formed by the photoconductor & the insulatory layers of the tape. This potential
is applied thru an electron flood beam, Contact is maintained for a period of
time equal to many times the series R-C circuit. At the end of this period, a
uniform potential difference equal to the applied voltage V is established
across the insulator layer, The electron flood beam is turned off and the
applied voltage reduced to zero. Tape is now ready for optical exposure Step 2-
Image is projected onto photoconductor, & simultaneously an electron beam makes
contact with surface of the insulator. Only potential diff. around equiv. circ
to that which has been stored in insulator. This charge in insulator can now
decay towards zero where optical image is brighter, photo conductor resistance
is lowest and potential decay 3/22/61 MW 3/20/61 LW

### Page 112
will be most rapid. An electrostatic charge image corresponding to optical image
is now fixed in insulator layer. Beam scan to reproduce. Magna Tech Electronic
Co. 630 9th Ave, N.Y. 36 Film-sound prodn equipt Oct 1960 Issue-Fiber Optics

Note regarding Interference No. 91657 with Olin Mathieson Chemical Corporation.
I called Mr. Mahler, patent attorney for Olin Mathieson in N.Y.C- last fall and
last January in this matter and suggested that we get together and discuss this
matter. In our conversation he asked about my other interference (91656)
involving Reynold Metals & myself and I told him I did not intend to contest the
matter with Reynolds since I know them to have been ahead of me. Now I have been
notified by the Patent Office that the interference procedure has been
terminated due to Olin Mathiesons filing under Rule 456 to drop one of their
co-inventors. I.R.E. Show - While at this show on Thursday , Mar. 23rd I talked
to a salesman of Powertron Ultrasonics Corp, Roosevelt Field, Garden City, L.I.,
N.Y. after noticing their Ultrasonic level control in action. I conceived of
this being used for liquid metal level control and discussed this with him
including the following conceived ideas which I intend to file a patent on. The
Ultrasonic probe is coupled to the exterior surface of the mold or flow chamber
into or through which liquid metal is flowed and senses the level of the liquid
metal. 4/18/61 MW

### Page 114
In this way the probe need not contact the liquid metal. The salesman said he
had not heard of such an application and that the transducer or probe was
guaranteed for operation to only 500° F. However upon questioning him, I
discovered that Powertron's transducer is a welded, not epoxy resin bonded,
assembly and that it is magnetostructrally operated. Therefore I stated that it
could be calibrated above 500° F for high temperature operation and that the
transducer and/or mold could be liquid cooled if necessary to reduce its
temperature. I told him that I would that in touch with his company regarding
this and my other near ultrasonic devices for possible licensing. I also
conceived of an application to a casting wheel where the ultrasonic transducer
is movable on an arm to contact the exterior surface of ~~ the ~~ a mold of a
plurality of wheel mounted molds at the level desired in casting to sense the
metal when it reaches said predetermined level, and provide a signal to effect
termination of metal flow by control of a servo regulating flow which transducer
then retracts off the mold permitting rotation of the wheel. The arm mounting
the transducer to be coupled to the mold is driven by a first servo means
towards and away from the mold and is prepositioned in height to account 4/18/61
MW

### Page 115
for different liquid levels  of different  to be attained in different molds by
a second servo means which is programmed and operated in accordance with the
rotation of the wheel to selectively preposition said probe at different heights
for each mold to effect casting to a predetermined level in each mold. In other
words, the height posited is servo adjustable to permit the ultrasonic probe or
transducer to be prepositioned at a selected height for each mold prior to
coupling engagement with the mold. Jerome Lemelson March 24, 1961 I visited Mr

May 23, 1961 I visited Epoxy Products Company (a Division of Joseph Waldman and
Sons, Irvington N. J.) ~~ I spok ~~ to obtain samples of their conducting epoxy
adhesive material. Mr. Norman J. Gallop, Technical Sales Representative
introduced me to their chief chemist Mr. Sussman and spoke with their chemist
doing research ( named Dick) on the subject. In my discussions with their chief
chemist, I asked if they had tried to use copper or aluminum powders as filler
conductor materials rather than silver which is quite expensive. When they
informed me that they had not been successful with these due probably to the
oxide film which forms on the surface of the particles, I remarked that perhaps
these materials could be used if they were mixed with the plastic either
immediately after forming prior to becoming oxidized or if they were kept rom
oxidizing by forming them (by flame spraying) in an inert atmosphere free of
oxygen or oxidizing material. He, Mr. Sussman, stated that this would be a
research project on itself Since this appears to me to be a worthwhile project I
intend to file a patent application on the method of producing conducting
plastics by forming oxygen free copper, aluminum or lead powders and retaining
them oxygen free while mixing them with an epoxy resin or other suitable LW
5/24/61 5/26/61 MW THIS CONFIDENTIAL MATTER READ & UNDERSTOOD BY EJ Waldmeyer
DATE 5/24/61

### Page 138
resin as either a molding compond, adhesive, or powder combination of said

material such as nylon, filled with conducting powder which may be injection or
compression molded. I conceive of the possibility of doing this by utilizing
(mixing) silver or oxygen free copper or aluminum powders with finely divided
particles of plastic (thermoplastic) and molding the mixture by the application

computer over or by means of telephone lines. One application of such a device
and answerback equipment at the storage computer is to facilitate air lines, bus
or train reservations from a location remote from the storage drum or computer
where, for example, an agent currently must place a phone call to the office
containing the reservation storage device and ask a clerk there at to operate an
input device to derive information from the computer. Other applications include
any function such as banking, etc, in which stored information may be
automatically requested over phone or telegraph lines. (inventory, order,

information, to him. Following assumptions are made. ~~ I.~~ It is assumed that
data is originally provided on a sheet of paper or card (punched or plain) and
that updating is effected by typing or otherwise entering information on one or
more lines provided below those on which information has already been entered,
as in standard bookkeeping practice. Each document is of standard, predetermined
size and all lines and columns of alphanumericical entries  are have

System No. 5. 7/9/62 Aspects of system #5 include: 1. Video picture signals
(picture plus sync and blanking components) recorded in tandem array on magnetic
tape. 2. Frame identifying signals (preferably binary) recorded on adjacent
channel(s) of tape. 3. Signals identifying ordinate band areas of each frame
(areas on each of which a line of alpha-numeric characters may be recorded such
as a monthly accounting entry) may be or is recorded. (These signals may be
single pulse signals occupying a single track of the magnetic tape. 4.

(identifying the video picture signal portion derived in scanning the line-band

between ~~ to either March 6, 1962 Stamp Dispensing Cash It is conceived to
provide a cash register which, when the amount of a sale is entered, disenses
the correct amount (monetary value) of trading stamps or premium certificates.
This dispenser mechanism may either be mounted integrally within the register
housing and adapted to dispense stamps provided in coils within the housing
through an opening just open the cash drawer or at the side of the register (for
the customer to remove), or the dispenser may be mounted in its own housing at
the side of the cash register housing, which dispenser housing is removable and
replaceable as a unit for repair. (It is also conceived to provide stamps in
their own plastic housings or cartridges which cartridge need merely to be
inserted into an opening in the dispenser housing and removed when the stamps
are used up). (over) LER 5/23/62 EL 3/31/62 JC 4/9/62 THIS CONFIDENTIAL MATTER

A motor vehicle is driven by a chain conveyor underneath a plurality of frames
or stations. Prior to station A is the area A', a plurality of cleaning stations
including detergent and water sprays may be provided to wash the dirt off the
car, and if necessary to effect at least partial drying of the body (with air

vehicle body, the action being triggered manually or by a limit switch or
photoelectric detecting the vehicle. At station B, buffing drums C & D mounted
on counterbalanced rotating frames C' and D' buff and polish the applied wax At

Method of Molding: (previous page) Steps (Process #1) (1) Laminate decorated
film of plastic to extruded or calendered base sheet. (2) Cut to predetermined
shape (cut out disc, square, round, oval, etc) from sheet. (3) Lay against mold
half over cavity of compression mold. (4) Heat by induction to soft condition
(5) Compress other mold half against upper surface of cut-out form to mold it to
shape without substantial distortion of the decoration except where
compartmental walls, ribs, etc. form. Above many be accomplished automatically
by feeding a decorated sheet onto a flight conveyor containing molds (preferably
machined into flights and compressing second conveyor flights or ram operated
mold sections against sheet to force it into molds of flight conveyor. Jerome

electron beam

to traverse the melt and zone refine the metal, and using either the same

- Character Reader The following improvements in my character optical reader
using optical matching employing character shaped openings in a rotating disc
are conceived: (1) Magnetostrictive oscillation of the disc in the plane of the

scanning system such as a lens, prism etc to effect the results of (1.) (3)

July 24, 1962 I. Plating & Coating It is conceived to plate or diffusion coat
metal, ceramic or other material by scanning the surface thereof with laser
light to heat said surface and using the same or another laser light to vaporize
or heat the coating material(s). The coating or plating material may be
vaporized immediately adjacent the surface being coated and deposited thereon by
(a) electro-deposition in which the work is negatively charged and/or the
material (rod or powder) being vaporized positively charged or less negative
than the work; (b) by flow induced by the intense light beam, (c) by flow of the
vapor induced by a gas such as an inert gas directed as a stream against the end
of the rod or material being vaporized, (d) by electromagnetic force induced
adjacent the material being vaporized, etc If the plating or coating material is
a powder, it may be continuously introduced as a stream against the surface to
be coated which is being and preferably has been heated by the laser light beam
which also scans and heats the powder to melt and/or vaporize it immediately
adjacent the work surface The material being plated or coated may either be
sprayed or flowed against the surface of the article to be coated LW 8/1/62 E.T

Sept 21, 1962 Method and Apparatus for Producing Multi-Colored, Decorative
Extrusions It is conceived to produce tubing ~~ of ~~ strips, sheet or other
shapes of plastic in a plurality of colors and decorative effects on a
continuous basis by the following method: (a) A shape (tubing, strip, angle,
sheet, slate, etc) is first extruded consisting of a major portion of a first
colored plastic and having a longitudinal portion, portions or all of its
exterior surface covered or coated with a thin layer (.001 to .005 inches thick
or more) of the same or a different plastic preferably of a different color. For
example, the entire exterior surface of a cylindrical (tube or rod) extrusion
made of a first colored plastic or a band portion thereof may be extruded with
or extrusion coated with a thin layer of a plastic of a different color. Or a
sheet or plate of one color (white, yellow, etc) of plastic may have a coating
or extruded-on layer on one or both surfaces of a second color (red, black,
blue, etc.) The extruded-on coating is such that, if an embossing tool such as
an embossing drum or drums with a predetermined pattern or patterns thereon is
brought against said coating (preferably shortly after exiting from the
extrusion die), the material of the thin THIS CONFIDENTIAL MATTER READ &
UNDERSTOOD BY Jules Cotler DATE 9/21/62 THIS CONFIDENTIAL MATTER READ &
UNDERSTOOD BY BJM DATE THIS CONFIDENTIAL MATTER READ & UNDERSTOOD BY EL DATE
10/16/62 THIS CONFIDENTIAL MATTER READ & UNDERSTOOD BY JBG DATE Oct 14, 1962

### Page 74
coating will be seperated or spread laterally leaving breaks or openings in the
coating in accordance with the designs of the embossing die and thereby
providing a sheet or other extruded shape with ~~ an ~~ embossed designs in it
which show up in the color of the base material surrounded by the color of the
coating material. The technique may be used to number, letter or code pipe, rod,
wire covering, etc. or to decorate sheet plastic which may be used per se or
further formed as by vacuum forming, pressure forming, or other thermal forming
preferably on a continuous basis as it extrudes and after said embossed designed
have been provided therein. The thin coating may also be provided by

Dec. 20, 1962 A new type of electro-hydraulic computer is conceived which uses
one or more of the following phenomenon as working media (1) Liquid metal such
as mercury, gallium etc which can be controlled or reacted or both by fluid
control means (gates, valves, pistons, nozzles, orifices, jets of fluid, etc)
and by electrical means (electromagnetic forces, electron beams, spark
discharge, capacitance, resistence, etc) to provide a computing or control
system, subsystem or device utilization varcation in ~~ both ~~ electrical,
magnetic, fluid, and other forces in combination with each other (2) The working
medium may comprise or include a plasma fluid~~e~~ such as a highly ionized gas
or ~~ plasl ~~ plasma which may be operated on by a combination of means for
physically regulating, alerting or otherwise affecting fluid flow (gates,
valves, Pistons, diaphragms, nozzles, orifices, jets of fluid (same or other),
etc); magnetic means such as electromagnetic coils generating variable magnetic
JBG. THIS CONFIDENTIAL MATTER READ & UNDERSTOOD BY

### Page 125
fields which vary in accordance with changing parameters of the symptom being
controlled. The plasma may also be affected by forces generated by an electron
beam directed into said plasma and varied in accordance with a program or
changes in parameters of the system being controlled; by variations in the
make-up or densely of the plasma, by varying material used to dope the plasma;
possible by varying the capacitance between plates or electrodes placed in the
plasma stream; by varying the temperature of the plasma; by varying the
characteristics of spark discharge into the plasma, etc A stream or streams of
the plasma (2) or liquid metal (1) may be further controlled as to direction,
shape, mass flow, amplification in addition to control effected by one or more
of the means described above by means as described in the first symposium on
Fluid Amplification (re. fluid amplifying devices announced by the Diamond
Ordnance Fuze Laboratories (Control Engineering Nov. 1962 p. 21) In other words,
A plasma will provide an excellent working medium for an electro-hydraulic
computing system since it can be made to behave as a fluid and be controlled

Dec. 29, 1962 Gyro-stabilizer for hand held cameras: It is conceived to provide
a hand-held motion picture camera with means for stabilizing a movable lens
system (or the camera itself) in the vertical direction ~~ once it in the ~~ to
home on an axis defined when the start switch is pushed (that ~~that~~ optical
axis which it has when the user first starts to take a picture) so that vertical
(small vertical) movements incurred thereto by unsteadiness of the operator (his
inability to hold the camera steady) will not cause the resulting photographic
phenomenon to appear as a jumpy motion picture. Perhaps the simplest arrangement
may be to stabilize a mirror or prism in the optical system receiving the light
thru the camera by means of a gyroscopic stabilizer of the type used to
stabilize a gun turret) The gyro may be driven by an electric motor powered by
the same batteries used to power drive the film through the camera and/or to
power operate the camera zoom lens and THIS CONFIDENTIAL MATTER WITNESSED &
UNDERSTOOD BY: DATE THIS CONFIDENTIAL MATTER WITNESSED & UNDERSTOOD BY: DATE

### Page 129
electric eye shutter. The gyro may be automatically coupled to the prism or
other assembly to be stabilized when the push button switch ~~ start ~~ used to
start the film drive is closed Uncoupling of the gyro-stabilizer from the
assembly ~~ slab ~~ to be stabilized may be effected automatically when the push
button switch is released or opened and for example, when the operator rocks the
push-button arm to the side to voluntarily effect said uncoupling when he
desires to shift the optical axis vertically. Rocking the depressed push button
arm may activate another switch or open a swich which is first closed when the
push button is depressed which action is operative to electrically effect
uncoupling by actuating a solenoid effecting uncoupling or rocking the push
button arm may be operative to effect mechanical uncoupling such as by
uncoupling a clutch between the output drive of the gyro-stabilizer or the part
or platform being stabilized. of course a second push button switch operated by
a second finger or by the manner in which the pistol grip for the camera is held
may also be used to effect coupling and uncoupling of the gyro-stabilizer and
the lens, mirror or prism assembly. THIS CONFIDENTIAL MATTER WITNESSED &

January 3, 1963 BEN KINBERG ASSOCIATES Invested Ben Kinberg today and we
discussed toy guns including my patents for RICOCHET Guns. He asked me if I had
any ideas for marketing guns and I informed him that Darsey Mfg Co produce smoke
with oil but that it could also be clone with powder such as take if the powder
could be metered through a small hole so that it would last long enough and
would not dispense too much at one time. I conceive of a construction in a toy
gun in which a chamber is provided (preferably above the main barrel of the gun)
with dowardly tapering walls to feed the powder and a slanting bottom wall which
terminates at a small opening which is normally closed off by the piston  in the
barrel or bore on by a small pin serving as a valve operation of the trigger
and/or movement of the piston or other device in the barrel such as a spring
operator ball or bullet ejector is effective in lifting the pen in a manner to
effect two actions, CM 1/3/63 THIS CONFIDENTIAL MATTER WITNESS & UNDERSTOOD DATE

### Page 135
(1) the hole in the bottom wall opens and (2) the powder in the general vicinity
of the opening is agitated so that a small quantity flows downward into the bore
of the barrel and/or onto a portion of the piston front face so that when the
piston moves forward and stops, the powder will be thrown off by inertia. The
powder may also be dispensed onto the missile being fired so that it trails
behind when the missile fired and is dispensed by the turbulent air behind the
missile. Or it may be depressed onto the bottom wall of the bore to be picked up
by the piston in its forward travel. Or, the operator may dispense powder onto
the missile (unto a retaining groove or shelf at the rear end of the missile,
prior to loading) Smoking toys using the above arrangements are conceived as
follows (a) A water gun which smoke, (b) A ball or bullet firing gun which
smokes (c) Cap firing gun which smoke (d) Suction cup dart gun smoke (e) Spring
operated action toy smoke. (f) Motor driven toy which smokes.

student)and (c) automatically score or tabulate the results of the test. One or

back for teaching or questioning when passed to a loudspeaker If the tape is run

until the next question is asked to answer the previous question. Answers are
multiple choice and each student has a black box with two or more push-button
switches for selectively answering questions. Answers are recorded in one of ~~
two ~~ several manners. In a first means, each person ~~ is ~~ has a certain
number of recording channels with each channel operatively connected to a
respective push button of his black box. When one of the push buttons is
depressed, a signal is recorded on the channel associated therewith. The correct
answer is preferably provided either as a particular frequency recording on an
adjacent channel or as a particular location recording. After the test has been
completed, the tape is re-run (forward or in reverse) and logical circuits are
used to total the correct and/or incorrect answers. ~~ F In a second means, the
answers of each test participant are recorded as specific codes on one channel
of the tape assigned to the participant. The channel also contains a location
code at the start of each length assigned to an answer code which location code
identifies the question for later analysis. THIS CONFIDENTIAL MATTER WITNESSED &

Plastic Form For Pouring Concrete Pillars: Most concrete pillars for buildings
and bridges which are poured in place are supported by wooden frames or
cardboard tubes. Both involve costly methods Several design for plastic concrete
pouring forms are conceived as follows: (a) The wall of this form is made of an
extruded plastic such as medium or high density polypropylene, polyethylene,
urethane, vinyl etc which is extruded as an open tube having preferably parallel
and either adjacent or overlapping edges capable of being secured together in a
manner to prevent the flow of concrete, cement or whatever material is being
poured. Securing of said edges may be effected by means of zipper strips secured
to said edges, fasteners adhesive tape, extruded weldedon lock joint portions
along the edge; steel strapping, separate strips of sealing extrusions, heat
sealed tape, etc provided that the sealing means is capable of removal or
opening without destroying the ability of the sheet ~~to~~ or form to be reused
(b) A second form is conceived which is made of THIS CONFIDENTIAL MATTER READ &
UNDERSTOOD BY

polypropylene, etc which will form a cylinder when the walls thlongitudinal

therealong formations which permit the edges to lock and seal when forced
together. During and after pouring, tape, steel strapping, buckled belting or
the like may be employed around the cylinder at spaced distances along its
length to prevent separation of the locked or frictionally retained edging. The
special edging may also be a zipper closure, or separately extruded members of

removed If the sheeting has a coating of synthetic flexible rubber or

FOR EXAMINING TEETH using ultrasonic energy. It is conceived to place a small
instrument or housing in the mouth of a ~~ patient ~~ patient for automatic
scanning of the teeth to replace X-ray methods. It is also conceivable that an
infra-red scanner may be employed outside of the mouth to obtain an image on the
face of a cathode ray tube (as with the ultrasonic scanner) of the teeth since
bone material (of which the teeth are made) radiates heat at a different
wavelength than skin (human). It is possible that a combination of infra-red
scanning and ultrasonics may be employed to replace X-ray. JL 2/5/63

scanning techniques. Either or both may employ filling the mouth with water. For

Photoelectric Toys A design arrangement is conceived whereby a wheeled vehicle
or otherwise motor driven vehicle or target fixed object contains a
photoelectric cell and control the operational circuit control and battery
components are remotely connected, potentiated in a housing and are electrically
connected to the vehicle or target object by one flexible wire and potentiating
means such as a self moving cam & brushes. The advantage here is that the
vehicle need not be weighted down with all the components. A different vehicle
target or toy may be pluggable to the photoelectric cell of the single
controller. The photoelectric device may also be in a pluggable housing so that
is easily disconnectable from the toy vehicle.

(Schenectady, N.Y.) has just announced (p.70 Chemical week, Jan 26-63) the
development of a new lubricant additive, which, when applied to the extrusion of
aluminum, results in extruded shapes with a mirror finish. It may also be
applied to give bright finishes in processes such as die forming, roll forming,
rolling, wiredrawing, polishing, etc. The following fabricating methods ~~ emplo
~~ and articles utilizing or employing such new additive are conceived by me: 1.
A method and apparatus for extruding sheet, tubing, angles, and and other shapes
with mirror surface finishes combined with one or more of the following
processes derived by guiding the extrusion as it extrudes through one or more
stations containing apparatus set-up downstream of the extruder in line with the
extrusion die for: a) anodizing the extrusion to protect and retain the mirror
finish; CM 2/13/63 E.L. 2/20/63

### Page 158
(a) Plastic coat the outside and/or inside of the extrusion ~~ prw after or
without anodizing. The hot extrusion may be cooled by fluid means (by passing it
through a cooled liquid, blasting air thereagainst, etc) to the molten range of
the plastic (if thermoplastic) and thereafter guided through special rubber
grommets (the shape of the extrusion) provided in the side walls of bins in
which a powder of the thermoplastic plastic is fluidized which forms a coating
thereon or said plastic may be sprayed, roller coated or applied by extrusion
wrapping it ~~ a strip around the extrusion which melts on the hot metal and
later fuses forming a coating; by passing the extrusion thru grommets in the
sidewalls of a bin containing liquid plastic, by electro-statically applied
powder or spray, etc. (c) Continuously straighten the extrusion as it comes out
of the die by servo controlled stretching the extrusion so that it will not have
to be straightened after receiving a coating or anodizing (d)Process the
extrusion before it oxidizes by means such as provided on pp 69-75, p. 34
(electron beam or light beam decorative machining of the surface of the
extrusion)

determined by: (i) the shape of the tool, brush or buff operating on the surface
of the extrusion as it extrudes (ii) a mask in the form of a closed loop

include (a) Dies, rollers, slide-ways, bearings, etc having the lubricant or

material to be coated. Compressing the article into the die (with or without

the article. The pressure may be such (as may temperature) as to cause the
powder to melt into a non-porous coating or to provide a porous coating with
lubricant filling the pores. J. Lemelson Caroline Murray 2/13/62 Feb. 13–1963
Continuing with the above lubricant additive and its polishing effects, the
following methods and articles have also been conceived: 2. A method for coating
an article with aluminum or other metal and creating a mirror finish on the
coating are conceived as follows: (a) Completely coat the surface of a rod or
wire, strip or sheet with metal such as aluminum. Then pass the coated piece
thru a drawing die lubricated by said G.E. additive with the diameter of the die
being slightly smaller than the diameter of the coating. In other words, the die
is not used to drawing the wire but only to smoothen the surface of the coating
and to impart final mirror finish thereto. E.L. 2/20/63 CM 2/25/63

### Page 162
otherwise, since the base were itself (if steel coated with aluminum) is not
being drawn, the coating material will only be drawn and perhaps removed from
the base. Diameter of the die will depend on such variables as uniformity of
coating, amount of surface working required to create mirror finish, etc.
Process may be continuous in which single line or pass is used to coat the wire,
draw it thru a die, then anodize or plastic coat the polished surface of the
coating. Heat of coating and/or drawing may be used to enhance or improve
anodizing or for plastic coating. Automatic temperature controls, means for
lowering or raising temperature where necessary, etc may be applied to
continuous process. Anodizing may be effected or enhanced by incorporating
anodizing chemicals in lubricant used for drawing and either connecting the die
or dies and/or other surfaces such as rollers (conducting rubber rollers)
contacting the wire as it is drawn in circuit with the necessary source of
electrical energy to effect anodizing of the polished surface of the coating.

Feb/3/63 It has been conceived by me for some time to clean clothing and the
like by a process which includes the following steps and apparatus (a) Apply
cleaning fluid to the clothing by soaking or spray either prior to and/or after
admitting said clothing to a drum adapted to rotate about a horizontal
(longitudinal) EL 2/20/63 CM 2/25/63

### Page 166
axis. (b) at one end of the drum is placed an ultrasonic sirene or whistle
adapted to generate intense sound waves within the drum as it rotates tumbling
the clothes (c) The ultrasonic whistle has the effect of removing the cleaning
fluid from the clothing and removing dirt therewith which has been dissolved in
said fluid. The hypersonic sound waves generated in the air/vapor surrounding
the clothes in the drum may also be operative to react with cloth or fabric of
the clothing so as to shake dirt, loosened by the cleaning fluid, off the
clothing (d) If liquid (cleaning fluid) is admitted to the drum either prior to
and/or after starting the ultrasonic sirens, the clothes which are tumbled by
being carried to the top of the drum, will fall freely thru space to be
subjected to high intensity sound waves and will thereafter fall into the liquid
to be drenched again to continue the process (e) The apparatus would include a
sequential controller such as a multicircuit timer for automatically EL 2/20/63

Rubber or Flexible Plastic with Structure improving its gripping ability
Following designs are conceived to improve the ability of rubber or synthetic
rubber to grip road or floor. May be used in tires, on shoe soles or heals, in
rubbers where use may be on ice or snow or other slippery surface. 1. Rubber
Containing Curled Filaments Filaments may be plastic monofilaments, metal
fibers, filaments or curled wires, etc. which are either bonded to the surface
of the rubber article by spraying on plastic such as urethane to adhere the
filaments thereto and possibly continuing to build up a layer of plastic to
encapsulate the filaments completely or just leave a certain amount protruding
therefrom. Filaments may be applied as a matte or sheet or may be chopped or
broken and applied as roving to the surface which is either Sponge Cells CM
3/13/63 E.L. 3/11/63

### Page 186
plastic coated or semi molten. Filaments may be compressed against surface
between plates or rollers or merely weighted by the plastic or urethane rubber
applied by spraying. Filaments may be mixed with plastic or rubber prior to
molding or extruding into article. Filaments may comprise a matte with grit
bonded to individual filaments such as Scotch-Brite scouring matte. If filaments
are metal wire or wool it may be welded to a metal base sheet (spot or line
resistance welding by compression between welding dies) after which liquid
urethane or other plastic may be sprayed, roller coated or molded against and
into the filaments so welded. Fine grit may be added to the plastic to be molded

trading cards, etc J Lemelon Hydraulics Extension - (impacting with hydraulics)
Reference is made to the process of extruding metal by the direct application of
a hydraulic fluid within the extrusion chamber to the face of a bullet. In one
process a hydraulic fluid is applied both to the bullet face and to the
extrusion itself after it has come out of the extrusion die. It is conceived by
me to work the metal of the extrusion to improve its crystalline structure,
reduce porosity, eliminate defects therein, etc by either intermittently
applying pressure to the upstream fluid and/or downstream fluid in the form of
low frequency pressure valves and/or high frequency waves concurrent with the
low frequency waves. These pressure fluctuations or waves E.L. 3/11/63 CM
3/19/63

### Page 192
may be applied to the either or both upstream & downstream (before and after the
extrusion die) by one or more of the following techniques. (a) By opening and
closing valves extending to high and/or low pressure reservoirs, pumps, etc (b)
By starting and stopping pumps. (c) By spark discharge inside the fluid system
(intermittent spark) (d) By exploding wire, exposives, etc inside fluid system
(e) By means of an ultrasonic transducer(s) inside or coupled to fluid system &
this includes magneto structure rods, vibrating crystal, etc (f) By means of
creating and collapsing magnetic fields in the fluid and/or surrounding the
billet. Billet itself may be expanded and collapsed by electromagnetic fields
applied thereto and/or the die or extrusion chamber to both directly affect the
extrusion and/or create shocks in the fluid on either a both sides of the billet
and extrusion which shock waves propagate and reflect against the walls of the
chamber and off the extrusion itself METHOD OF CONTINUOSLY HYDRAULICALLY
EXTRUDING &/or working metal (over) EL 3/11/63 CM 3/13/63

### Page 193
A number of processes for the continuous extrusion of metal are conceived, viz:
(a) Continuously cast metal to a first shape, then draw or extrude it
continuously through a die to a second shape. Metal so drawn or extruded may be
further worked by means described above and/or as described in my pending patent
application. (b) Continuously form powdered metal (by spraying, spark or
evaporation techniques and continuously extrude said powder to predetermined

substantially conforming to the shape of the wall of the chamber. Material such
as powdered ceramic, metal or slugs to be extruded is admitted to chamber volume
13 thru a valve means 17 communicating with 13 thru opening 18. After admission
of a charge, the material is compacted against the die 20 by advancing the
piston 14and heat may be applied by means of induction coil means 11 at the end
of the chamber to melt or sinter mass 19. A sub-piston valve 15 is provided in
piston 14 to permit a liquid such as liquid metal, high temp hydraulic fluid
etc. to be admitted to chamber volume 13 after the piston is withdrawn.
Thereafter a combination of direct high pressure applied to the fluid behind the
slug or mass 19 and shock waves applied to the fluid are used to force the metal
thru die opening 20'. Notation 21 refers to a chamber downstream of the die
which may also be pressurized to support the die during extrusion. Pressure
fluctuations or shocks may be applied to the fluid in region 22 in synchronized
relation to the pressure variations applied to the fluid in region 13 to both
reduce stresses on the die and/or act to compact the material being extruded to

Method of Testing Material (and Articles) A previous disclosure related to
applying a magnetic field to an article and analyzing the results on the
material thereof. The following are conceived variations in this method. 1.
Suddenly applying an intense magnetic field to an article to cause it to become
stressed and change its dimension. Analyzing its internal characteristics by one
or more of the following means applied either simultaneously or seperately in a
predetermined order and time interval, (a) Ultrasonic inspection, pulse-echo or
waves passed thru the material as it is magnetically stressed, before and
immediately thereafter. (b) Infra-red scanning of material (either using its own
material heat emissions or internally applied heat (c) X-ray inspection (d)
Surface wave analyses (e) Strain gage analyses (over)

EL 3/22/63 CM 3/13/63

### Page 211
(f) electron microscope analyses of a crystalline structure during, before and
after strain. (temporary or permanent deformation) (g) other means such as
spectral analyses. ~~ etc ~~ electron optics, etc 2. Applying an intense
magnetic force to a portion of an article and applying one or ~~ of ~~ more of
1(a) to (g) above technique. 3. Applying an intense magnetic force to an article
portion and comparatively analyzing signals or optical images of stressed
portion with other portions by photographing, scanning, etc. Digitizing and
computer analyzing the results. 4. Applying an intense magnetic field to an
article, recording the output signal generated by one or more of the transducers
associated with 1a to 1g above and analyzing the signal by comparing it with one
or more analog signals deriveved for example, from scanning either an unstressed
article of the same shape and material or with a signal derived from ~~ stress
~~ magnetically stressing and scanning (as in 1a to 1g above) a standard article
of similar shape CM 3/13/63 EL 3/23/63

PLASTIC FABRICATION PROCESSES & APPARATUS The following processes involve the
continuous extrusion of the thermoplastic materials such as polyethylene,
polypropylene, etc. into plastic sheet or film and its continuous vacuum drawing
into molds or containers for the purposes of (a) forming articles such CM
3/26/63 EL 3/30/63

### Page 236
as plastic bottles or tubes, (c) lining containers such as drums, cans, bottles,
paper, ~~or ~~corrugated or paperboard boxes. Methods & Apparatus include: I.
Continuously extrude or calender thermoplastic sheet, feed over or adjacent open
containers such as drums, boxes, cans, etc., clampingly engage the sheet against
the rim of the container and apply vacuum to the inside of the container (and/or
pressure above the sheet) while the sheet is semi-molten as the plastic sheet
being extruded and/or post heated, to draw the sheet into the container to form
a plastic liner, therefore which conforms to the shape of the container.
Containers are continuously fed on top of a belt conveyor or with the upper rim
of the container held by clamping means at the level of a belt or flight
conveyor parallel to the soft or semi-molten plastic sheet. Clamping of the
sheet against the rim may be effected by a second closed loop belt conveyor
disposed above the conveyor carrying the containers and above the sheet, or by a
flight of a closed loop flight conveyor. Vacuum may be applied to the inside of
each container to effect drawing the semi-molten sheet or film into the
container in one of several manners: viz(next page) CM 3/26/63 EL 3/30/63

### Page 237
(a) The container may be open at its lower end (i.e a bottomless can resting on
a conveyor flight which is later capped) (b) a small opening may be provided in
the lower end to which a conduit is attached  for applying vacuum. (c) the
bottom of the container may be porous or contain natural openings (i.e. folded
paper board carton, etc.) opening b) may be automatically closed off after so
leaving the containers. The left ( closed loop belt conveyor) on which the
container bottoms ride may be porous or made of screening capable of passing
air.  A plenum chamber from which air is constantly being withdrawn may be
placed beneath this belt in the vicinity of the location where the semi-molten
plastic sheet is drawn of the top of the container and the sheet will
automatically be drawn into the container when air i automatically drawn into
the plenum chamber through the belt from the inside of the container. An
apparatus is conceived in which the belt or flight conveyor carrying the
containers and (fired) the closed loop conveyr used to engage the plastic sheet
against the top of each container are adjustably movable away from each other to
accommodate containers of different heights. A method is also conceived CM
3/26/63 EL 3/30/63

### Page 238
in which the plastic sheet is not clampingly engaged against the open rims of
the containers but is merely brought thereagainst and drawn into the containers
by atmospheric pressure when vacuum is applied to the interior of the container.
Thus, additional plastic material from the surrounding sheet may be flowed into
the container (or mold) from the surrounding sheet of plastic and deeper draws
are possible without drawing the sheet to thin. For containers which do not have
bottom openings, air may be evacuated therefrom by the (automatic) insertion of
an open ended tube along the inside wall of the container from the open top
thereof to which tube vacuum is applied at the correct instant. After drawing
the plastic sheet to conform to the shape of the inside wall surface (and around
the then ~~ too ~~ tube, the tube is removed. A tool on pressure applied to the
container from the open end may be used to deform the plastic which conformed to
the tube shape or, the filling of the container thereafter with a product may
suffice to conform the lining to the wall, especially if the lining plastic is
flexible or thin. It is briefly noted that cap clamp CM 3/26/63 EL 3/30/63

### Page 239
a closure applied to the top of the container just prior to vacuum drawing may
be applied over the plastic sheet to dampingly engage it against the rim of the
container in place of the closed loop conveyor belt. These actions may all be
automatic J Lemelson all subject matter from page 177 to 212 Read & understood

### Page 273
Method and Apparatus for Continuously Producing Honeycomb on Waffle Sheering

Fig 1. In Fig. 1, metal powder or pellets 9 are discharged at a predetermined
rate from a hopper. Heated pellets of aluminium or other metal flow from the
hopper between two power driven drums 12 and 14, the exterior surfaces of each
of which are shaped with a plurality of projections or teeth disposed along the
length of each drum and adapted to fall between the side walls of the tooth-like
formations of the other drum (stations 13 and 16). The teeth do not mesh but
provide volumes 17 between the walls of each (see Fig. 2) which define the wall
thickness and shape of the resulting honeycomb cell or waffle-like sheet
structure.

### Page 274

Reynolds pellet process to form (a) Aluminum honeycomb (b)stampings-impact ext.
& (c) piston extrusion (intermittent)

Fig. 2 Fig. 3 Fig. 4

The forming teeth and spacing are illustrated in greater detail in Fig. 2 for
producing honeycomb structures with cells having thru and thru openings. Metal,
plastic, or other material is fed as pellets, powder, etc, or in other mixtures
capable of being compressed into a honeycomb (or other shape) panel, from the
top by gravity and is compressed to fill the cavities 17 defined by the rotating
teeth portion of drums 12 and 14. the greatest degree of compression which
defines the final shape of the panel where volumes 17 are the smallest, occurs
where the teeth are located along the adjacent radii which are CM 4/28/63 EL
4/23/63

### Page 275
substantially horizontal (ie those teeth which are closest together, metal as
pellets and or powder or other material flowed between the rollers is compressed
as it travels downward and the teeth come closer together. The amount of metal
necessary to provide a panel structure of the desired density and wall structure
will be a function of pellet size and shape which, in ~~lers ~~turn will depend
on the minimal volume 17 determined when the teeth are closest together. In
Figs. 1 and 2 the outer face of one tooth is shown completely abutting the
surface or base of its mating cavity in the other drum to provide thru & thru
opening to the panel cell. However, the structure illustrated in Fig 2 in which

JL 1/2/63 Apparatus and Method for Decorating Articles of Manufacture (Patent
application to be continuation-in-part of copending application entitled ) It is
conceived to decorate articles of manufacture such as molded plastic articles
(blow molded, injection molded, etc.) with multiple colors by the following
automatic process: (1) Preposition the article relative a means for generating a
first light pattern on the surface of the article after uniformly charging said
surface with a static electric field. (2) Project said first light pattern
against a predetermined. area of the article to create a charge pattern
according to the area(s) of the surface exposed to the light)(Electrons will be
repelled from the areas exposed to light; remain or gather in those areas not
exposed) (3) Dust or otherwise apply (such as by J Lemelson 1/2/63 THIS
CONFIDENTIAL MATTER READ & UNDERSTOOD

### Page 5
spray) particles of charged thermoplastic material of a first color (reference -
Material such as used in the X-erox, Haloid Co. process) against the surface of
the article which particles are attracted to and remain against the ~~ charge ~~
areas of the surface which are oppositely charged and are repelled from areas of
similar charge. (4) Heat (by radiant or other heating means) the first colored
particle to cause them to melt and become bonded to the surface in the applied
pattern) (5) Cool by removing said heat and/or convection means to fuse the
melted particles as solid areas of said first color. (6) Recharge the surface of
the article to give it a uniform static electric JL 1/2/63 THIS CONFIDENTIAL
MATTER READ & UNDERSTOOD BY THIS CONFIDENTIAL MATTER READ & UNDERSTOOD BY

1/2/63 charge pattern. (7) ~~ Ex ~~ Preposition either the article relative to a
second means for generating a second light pattern or the second means relative
the article (8) Generate and project said second light pattern against a
predetermined area or areas of the article to create a second charge pattern
different from the first on the surface of the article. (9) Dust or otherwise
apply particles or droplets of a charged thermoplastic material of a second
color against the surface of the article containing the second charge pattern
which particles are attracted to area(s) of opposite charge ~~ d ~~ and repelled
from areas of the same charge. (10) Heat the surface of the article JL 1/2/63

molding. By this method, a balloon (made preferably of silicone rubber or other

pressurized to confine the plastic as it expands or regulated its density. It
may also ~~ p ~~ be partly collapsed during molding. When the hollow article is
molded, the balloon may be deflated and removed, or retained within the
molding.)

Blow Molded Container & Method of Making It is conceived to produce a blow
molded box or bottle with an integrally molded cover, top or cap. In particular,
the container may be used to house such products as cigarettes(20 pack), cigars,
candy, etc. The method is applicable to the production of one piece, liquid
container also. A small rectangular box such as a cigarette box shape is
presented as an example to illustrate the method. In Figs. 1 and 2 is shown
details of a blow molded container 10 of rectangular parallepiped shape having
thin, sheet like plastic walls including a front wall 12, top wall 13, bottom
wall 14, rear wall 15 and side walls 16 and 17 which form a totally enclosed box
like container, after blow molding. The front wall 12 of the container 10 is
defined by an upper portion 12a and a lower portion 12b separated by a channel
like indicated formation 12c. CM 3/6/63

Methods and Apparatus for Identifying Articles Vehicles, Tokens and People
Automatically. A number of systems for identifying objects automatically have
been conceived. The following are general descriptions which will be expanded or
further described and developed. I. A card or flat token, preferably rectangular
in shape and dimensioned between one and two inches along ~~ a ~~each side. The
token contains a plurality of discrete value areas with indicia or other forms
of recordings, each of which value area when scanned and/or cancelled is the
equivalent in money expended ~~ of ~~ and represents payment by the user for
obtaining a particular product, monetary value in products, or service. For
example, the card or token may have 20 or 30 discrete areas each having a
predetermined location ~~ wl ~~and each when CM 3/6/63

scanned and/or cancelled by puncture or other means upon insertion into a
scanning device or machine, represents payment of a particular sum of money
towards, for example, payment of a train fare, road toll, admission to a
theater, etc. A specific example may comprise a card or toll representing a
commutation ticket ~~ for ~~good for 30 round trips on a vehicle such as a
train, bus, boat, or airplane and, as such would contain 60 discrete areas to be
scanned and/or cancelled by machine which upon positive identification of the
card and the uncancelled area thereof would result in opening a gate; unlocking
of a turnstile, release of a product, etc from a storage location etc. The card
may also contain recorded or shape means (edge notching) for identifying the
owner, date of purchase, etc. which may also be automatically scanned CM 3/6/63
THIS CONFIDENTIAL MATTER READ & UNDERSTOOD BY THIS CONFIDENTIAL MATTER READ &

Mar 6 - 63 Method & Apparatus for Producing Metal Beams, Bars, Tubing etc From
Continuously formed Metal Sheet. I. 1. Form sheet metal such as aluminum
continuously by extrusion, from powder pellets, etc. rolled. 2. Slit the wide
sheet into a plurality of strips on a continuous bases 3. Guide and convey the
strips thru rollers in a manner to cause them to abut and define a new shape 4.
Roll bond the strips together into said new shape. E Lobasco 4/16/63 CM 3/6/63

5. Steps 1 to 4 may be accompanied by folding or otherwise shaping one or more
   of the strips prior to welding it to the other(s) or by combining steel or
   other metal in the shape of wire strip, rod, etc with the new shape and/or by
   shaping the combined strips after they have been roll-bonded. Roll bonding or
   molecular welding of the strips may be supplemented or replaced by other
   forms of welding including induction, electron beam, ultrasonic, etc and may
   be accomplished by drawing the abutted strips through pressure welding rolls.
   Rolls and dies may be used to shape the new part. The strips may be butt, lap
   or otherwise welded together. Different degrees of surface areas of each
   strip may over-lap one or more of the other strips. II Tubing may be
   fabricated from continuously formed sheet EL 4/14/63

Kinberg Check A Word METAL SPINNING TECHNIQUES The following improvements in
metal spinning have been conceived. I. A method of spin forming a sheet or tube
of metal (or plastic or ceramic) comprising ~~ plac ~~ spin forming the metal to
a first shape in a lathe type fixture and thereafter drawing the metal while
spinning. Drawing may be effected by means of (a) moving a mandrel
longitudinally and axially against the spinning sheet after or during spin
forming or (b) in the case of a tube being spun to shape while the ends of the
tube are held in respective rotating chucks or fixtures, by power driving said
chucks or fixtures apart, preferably while a tool is depressed against the
surface of the spinning tube as to permit the metal EL 4/18/63

### Page 46
spin together to close & pour in metal onto plug

to draw out. Control of the movement and force exerted by the chucks in movement
away from each other as well as the force, location, and movement (radially as
well as longitudinally) of the tool or tools depressed against the tubing as it
spins, may be automatic in accordance with a program or other means. Control may
also be effected by means of feedback signals compared with recorded reference
signals and derived by optically or otherwise measuring the diameter of the
spinning part at the tool, the wall thinness thereof, the forces applied to the
tool, etc. II Form an article such as a drinking cup, pitcher, etc. by spinning

melting to atomize or vaporize. Methods and Apparatus For Continuously Extruding
Metal. The following steps are involved (Process#1) (a) Continuously form
pellets of metal such as aluminum (for example, by Reynold's metals technique of
pouring aluminum into a rapidly CM 4/28/63

### Page 57
rotating drum (e) The pelets are then screened, and reheated to a temperature
near the molten range of the metal - Thereafter, one or more of several
techniques may be employed to continuously extrude the pellets to a
predetermined shape. viz. I Pellets are fed to an extrusion screw at a flow rate
sufficient to permit said screw to force the pellets thru a die to form an
extrusion thereof Pellets may be heated in the extrude to a semi-molten state to
facilitate extrusion. Cut-off of lengths of the extrusion is on-the-fly. Screw
may reciprocate as it rotates to compact the pellets into a solid metal mass in
advance of the die. Employment of an intense expanding and collapsing magnetic
filed around in in the extrusion EL 4/23/63 CM 4/28/63

chamber may also solidify and densify the pellets into a solid extrudable mass.
II Pellets are fed to an extrusion chamber and are forced thru a die opening in
said chamber by a ram or piston. Piston advances toward die and retracts after
full forward motion permitting new charge of (heated) pellets - to enter
extrusion chamber in advance of ~~ it ~~ piston. Process repeats. Induction
energy applied to chamber and/or die heats charge and/or maintains temperature
of the end of ~~ the process ~~ what is left of the prior charge so that new
slug formed by a new charge unites with the remaining portion of the old charge
or slug. to form a single extrusion. Die may also be heated. CM 4/28/63

### Page 58
III Pellets are alternately charged first into one extrusion chamber (while the
other is extruding metal) then into the other. A valving means between the two
alternately feeds metal first from one and the other chamber to the die (and/or
~~ the ~~ a third chamber immediately in front of the die. Valving means may
comprise a rotating die plate. IV Pellets are fed downward between rollers which
are shaped to both roll and extrude the metal into various structural shapes
such as beams, channels, tubing, etc. Other rollers may be employed to further
shape the metal formed in the first rollers. V Pellets are automatically EL

(a) Model of Dust-Cloth made (b) light wt. hose & fitting (c) by-pass air
(adjustable vent) Dan Wyn (flasher & flash lite phone) Dust Cloth A model of my
vacuum dust cloth was completed on May. 6, 1963 and worked successfully (i.e.
was successful in picking up dust and face powder from surfaces) The model
consisted of a sheet of open cell urethane foam folded on itself with a Vexar
extruded netting sleeve inserted therebetween to maintain the foamed cellular
plastic portions apart - A vacuum cleaner head inserted at one end & connected
to a vacuum cleaner hose draw air thru the sponge or cellular cloth which picked
up dust. This was disclosed (drawings) to Al Landes and Marvin , on May 6, 1963
and I have ordered a larger section of stiffer Vexar from Du Pont to ~~
continual ~~ make a better model. Two improvements are conceived. ~~ (a) ~~ (a)
An adjustable opening at the inlet to the dust cloth or cellular plastic portion
would permit reduction of excess suction produced by the more powerful vacuum
cleaner. (b) Provision of a disconnectable section of light weight plastic
tubing to connect to the vacuum cleaner and to the dust cloth portions with
light weight end fittings. The present vacuum

PACKAGING MATERIALS The following packaging materials are conceived. (enlarged
several times or more)

FIG. 1 11 may be paperboard, corrugated cardboard, rigid plastic, foamed plastic
etc The packaging material 10 comprises a lamination of a base sheet 11 of paper
board, plastic or other suitable material which comprises the major thickness of
the p material 10. Coating one surface 13 of sheet 11 is a film 14 of heat
sealable plastic such as a polyvinyl chloride (Videne A) which may be extrusion
coated thereon. Laminated to film 14 and secured thereto by heat sealing is a
second film 15 of plastic sheeting material portions 15' of which stand off and
away from the coated surface 13 of sheet 11 to provide a quilt-like E.L. 5/13/63

(b) Sheet 15 may be passed through embossing rolls just prior to (or as)

the surface of the roll itself. If the embossing roll is properly heated, it may
shape 15 in a quilt-like pattern by engaging the sheet against a soft rubber
roll by means of said heated embossing roll without fluid vacuum or pressure.
(c) Sheet 15 may be vacuum formed to retain portions 15' away from the base 11

MACHINE A vending machine is conceived which will also fill and freeze EL
5/23/63

### Page 24
pouches, of plastic film with a liquid to provide frozen ice pops, cubes, or
other shapes of ice and the like for coin operated sales: General Description of
Machine & Operation 1. One or more roles of plastic film are provided in the
machine for dispensing a heat sealed strip of connected oblong plastic pouches
which extend laterally across the strip coming from the roll 2. Motor driven
guide and driven means engage the plastic pouch strip and feed it past a filling
device which contains an injector needle which injects a predetermined quantity
of liquid to be frozen into each pouch as it passes the filling station. A heat
sealing machine (optional) seals the hole created by the needle of the filling
injector 3. The still connected filled pouch is next driven through a freezing
chamber preferably containing thermoelectric freezing elements in which it may
be detained until ready to be dispensed. W 4. Upon insertion of a coin into the
machine and operation of a flavor selector, the end (filled and frozen) pouch of
the strip of pouches is

EL 5/23/63

### Page 25
severed from the strip by means of a cutting knife operated by a solenoid and
drops by gravity down a dispensing chute. Features and advantages of the machine
include: A. By providing concentrated sugar- flavor liquid or tablet mixes which
are automatically dispensed into a reservoir to provide a quantity of the liquid
(fruit-bar) to be frozen, the need for supplying large quantities of the liquid
product is eliminated - the machine merely need be connected to a water supply
and provided with automatic valves and controls to effect mixing of the
concentrated fruit or sugar juice prior to filling pouches therewith B. Use of
flat pouches in roll strip form ~~ permit ~~ plus liquid or powder concentrate
provides a large stock of the product to greatly increase the time between
machine filling. C. If the pouches are each pre-charged or contain ~~ powder ~~
small quantities of powder or liquid juice or sugar flavored mixture in
concentrated form, then it will only be necessary to inject water into each
pouch and agitate prior freezing.

EL 5/23/63

### Page 26
D. If it is desired to dispense connected, pre-filled pouches of juice bars
which are frozen in the machine, then the filled pouches may be guided and
driven by engagement of flat border strips at each end of the pouch
(longitudinal borders of the pouch strip) preferably containing a hole on each
border strip aligned with each pouch for sprocket drive thereof. The pouch strip
may be stored in a convoluting manner in a path thru which the strip will
automatically feed when first loaded after the strip is started by the service
man. Self threading strip may also apply to unfilled strip. (E) A BLOWER blowing
air thru the refrigerating zone may be used to cool the rest of the chamber
containing filled but not frozen pouches. (F) Control of filling may be effect
automatically by a counter whereby a batch or number of pouches are filled at a
time. Thus the end of the unfilled strip of pouches may be severed from a
predetermined number of filled pouches which are selectively dispensed
thereafter (G) Such a machine as described EL 5/23/63

### Page 27

for extruding film or pouches. (J) The pouches may be filled with water which is
frozen to produce ice for dispensary in cube form. The ice may also be chipped

soups, desserts, etc. may be similarly dispensed as above from either strips of

sheets in a predetermined strip pattern (c) bringing the other sheet against the

completely sealing off said duct to encapsulated said gas, and connecting

New Metal-Plastic Laminate It is conceived to provide new metal-plastic laminate
and to fabricate same into articles of manufacture therefrom as follows. I. Fig.
1 Fig. 2

The metal-plastic laminate 10 shown in Fig. 1 comprises a base sheet 11 of metal
such as aluminum or steel, to at least one surface 12 of which is is either
coated with a plastic layer 13 or is laminated to a first sheet 13 of plastic.
The sheet on coating 13 comprises a core material the upper surface 14 which is
laminated to or coated with a plastic sheet or layer 15 the upper surface 16 of
which may be embossed or otherwise decorated. The core layer ~~ of ~~ or sheet
13 comprises an unexpanded plastic containing a chemical which will release an
expanding gas, such as nitrogen which has the characteristic that the layer 13
will become blown or expanded into a cellular plastic layer such as 13
illustrated in Fig 2 This confidential matter witnessed &understood by EJW date

This confidential matter witnessed and understood by date

VM JC - 5/29/63 LW 6/9/63

### Page 70
Faber in which the outer spin or sheet 15 is lifted  of further away from the
metal base sheet 11. The laminate thus becomes more resilient or cushioned at
least to articles abutting the surface 16 of outer layer 15. The laminate 10 is
capable of being formed to a variety of shapes prior to expansion of the core
layer 13 by metal forming machinery such as die-presses, spinning machinery or
the like which would ordinarily damage or puncture the laminate to the expanded,
cellular layer 13' or would cause local collapsure  of  or buckling of said
layer. Bowls, trays, housing, seats, channels, angles and other structural
shapes applicable for the manufacture of furnature, appliances and the like may
be fabricated of sheets or strips of material 10.  after which  The core layer
13 may be expanded by passing the formed sheet metal part after it has been
formed to shape and in some instances after it has been assembled with other
parts, through an oven, adjacent radiant heaters or subjecting the metal layer
to means for generating heat therein by induction, electron beam or light beam
heating means. If heat is applied only to selected areas > JC -5/29/63 This

except 7, and 8. Jermone Lemelson Method of Molding Plastic is conceived whereby
two sheets of thermoplastic plaster which may be predecorated or plain as cast,
extruded or calendered are brought ~~ f into abutment ~~ face to face with each
other with a sheet of material disposed between the two and coated with a
release agent such as silicone or Teflon resins. The release resin coated sheet
may be a heating panel used to heat both sheets by conduction and/or radiation
to a semi-molten moldable state, the edging of both sheets is then clamped
together dry portions near the rims of respective molds or dies and air is
introduced between the sheets to below them into respective mold cavities. After
forming and cooling, the molds are removed (rotated) from the vicinity of the
sheets and the ~~ shee ~~ deformed positions of the sheets are brought together
and heat sealed to form hollow articles or die cut per se from the sheet of
which they are formed. EL 6/11/63 LW 6/9/63 THIS CONFIDENTIAL MATTER WITNESSED &
