1963 Electric Typewriter An electronic typewriter is conceived employing an
image forming device such as Hughes Aircraft Company's Charactron Tube to
provide an image on a screen (or tube face) in front of the typist. of what is
being typed. as it is typed preferably without employing type key impressions on
paper. The typewriter keys are each connected to respective switch or switching
controls operative when the particular key is depressed, to cause the beam of
the Charactron tube to deflect in a manner to cause the generation of the
respective alpha-numeric character at the correct position on the image screen
of the tube which would be equivalent to where the character would next fall if
it were typed on a page of paper. Controls accessible to the hand of the
operator would also be provided to effect one or more of the following functions
(see next page) EJW 7/20/63

### Page 100
(a) Erasure from the image tube of any particular character or characters such
as misspellings,miss-typings, etc. (b) Replacement of erased characters with
corrected or selected characters. (c) ~~ Era ~~ Rapid erasure of entire lines or
sentences. Shifting of remaining lines to fit the void spaces shifting of words
or characters. (d) Shifting of an entire paragraph,page,etc., to improve or
change its location on a page. (e) Generation of different images on a page in
relation to the typed material such as letterhead, photographs, sketches,
drawings, preprinted arrays of characters, etc. This function may be effected by
means of an erasable memory and key section of images at the typewriter keyboard
used to generate the alpha-numeric characters or by use of an electro-optical
system in which the image(s) to be added to the tube face is produced by video
camera scanning a photograph, sketch or print and written into a selected area
of the image tube face. (over) EJW 7/20/63

### Page 101
(f) Generation of one or more lines or paragraphs of alpha-numeric characters
onto a selected area of the pages (or tube face) from a memory such as from
paragraphs, letters, etc., by push-button selection from the memory. (g) The
production of hard copy of both one or any selected number of pages by what the
image which has been completed on the face of the character tub by push button
section using the Thermofax, Apecs or other wet or dry hard copy producing
system receiving an optical image of said tube face. (h) The push button (or
otherwise) selection of portions of the image on the tube face and the
production of one or a selected number of hard copies thereof (such as of the
heading of the letter on the face (4) of an envelope to serve as address
therefore (i) The push button entry of the image on the face of the Charactron

SCANNING SYSTEM It is conceived to effect more efficient transmission of
facsimile information over telephone lines as follows: (a) Utilize a dual system
of scanning rate. Control to scan a particular image field, that is provide a
first osculator system at both sender and receiver to which is operative to
drive both the read-beam of the video camera at the sending station and the
write beam of the video receiver at the sending station at a first speed and a
second oscillator a beam sweep speed control means at both sending and receiving
stations which is operative to drive the beams at a much higher speed. (b)
Automatically sense by scanning or other means the presence of an area lens in
the path of the picture or image field scanning beam of the camera prior to
arrival of said image field scanning beam threat. The area so sensed may be any
image intensity which is other than a white or redundant background and may be
sensed by a second beam or the leading edge of the scanning beam. sensing WW
7/20/63

### Page 104
may be effected by clipping the picture signal generated by the scanning beam
above or below a certain intensity, (frequency or amplitude)level and generating
a signal therefrom which is utilized to switch the output of the slow or fast
rate oscillator to control the beam sweep speed both at the sending and
receiving stations. In other words, both read and write beams are caused to scan
slow (or at conventional 30 frame/second speed) ~~ which ~~while scanning image
information which is not ~~ no ~~of predetermined intensity such as either white
or black background images, and are caused to scan faster (perhaps several times
30 frames/sec. speed or more) while scannning redundant field information (white
or black background)which field intensity is ~~ab~~ automatically genterated at
the receiver by automatic means if necessary. When the sensing beam no longer
senses an image area of a predetermined intensity or intensity range the lack of
an output signal therefrom is utilized to gate( by use of a monostable switch in
the output of the fast rate oscillator circuit driving the beam)the output of
the ~~ slow~~fast rate of oscillator to drive ~~the ~~ both beams at said EJW

### Page 105
faster rate. The sensing signal is thus not only generated at the scanning
camera and used to control the speed of the read beam thereof but is also
transmitted to the receiver station and used to and control the speed of
write-beam of the video picture tube (image tube) thereat so that the position
of both beams will always be in synchronized relationship to each other
regardless of how the read beam is speeded up or slowed down during scanning a
particular field - In other words the sensing signal is used to sync the
position and speed of sweep of the write beam with that of the read beam as well
as to effect control of the speed or rate of scanning of the two beams. It is
noted that the two oscillator systems must be synced to each other with the fast
sweep oscillator control generating line vertical sync signals at a frequency
which is a multiple of the frequency of that in which the slow rate oscillator
operates or the operation may be such that the fast sweep oscillator is only
operative to control the speed of the beam sweep and not line frequency which is
controlled either by a separate oscillator or the slow sweep oscillator
circuits. If the image field contains a line image of a particular intensity
along, for example, the right hand border, EW 7/20/63

FIG. 1 FIG. 2 the scanning of said line image may be utilized to generate a
signal (by clipping & differintiating the video picture signal) which signal may
be used as the line sync signal to return the beam to the next scanning line at
both camera and receiver. EJW 7/20/63

Fluid Jet - breaker Fluid Jet - R bond

Fluid Jet Devices Reference is made to fluid systems in which a small jet of
fluid such as air or other gas or liquid is used to control the direction of a
larger jet or stream of fluid from one path or passageway to another. The
following applications of such a system are conceived. I. Application to
electrical switching including circuit breaker applications. It is conceived to
generate a large flowing stream of fluid and utilize same to cool electrical
components of an operating electrical system by flow over and thru said
components. The stream is switchable to a passageway leading to one or more
cavities containing switch contacts or mechanical means for opening (or closing)
said contacts when fluid from said stream is diverted to said passageway leading
to said cavity or contact closing device. The ~~ div ~~ stream used to divert
the larger stream may be generated by valving fluid from the large stream using
electromechanical means, spring means, manual means, servo motor means, etc.
Also an exploding squib, wire, arc, etc may be used to generate the EJW 7/20/63
LB 8/15/63

### Page 113
smaller stream used to divert the larger stream from its general flow path to
the path leading to the switch closure ~~ means ~~ (or opening) means. The use
of a shock wave generated by a spark or exploding device may be used in general
apparatus employing the switching of one or more fluid streams to effect a
particular function and will provide more rapid stream switching. Also, a fluid
accumulator having pressurized fluid which is suddenly released in one or more
passageways of secondary ~~ flu fluid for generating diverting streams, may be
utilized in which fluid is released from the accumulator by solenoed, diaphragm

parts to engage & release the housing may suffice. (b) Provide hermetic sealing
for the assembled housing and for a quick connection to the rechargeable battery

15, 1963 Apparatus and Method for Continuously casting (or extruding) metal and
continuously coating or treating the shape so cast or extruded as it experiences
from the mold or die. viz. I. Continuously cast or extrude hollow shapes such as
pipe and introduce the coating material as a liquid or powder through the
mandrel (and/or an extension thereof extending some distance into the interior
of the shape being cast or extruded) in a manner to cause said material to form
the desired coating on the inside surface of the pipe. Note: the mandrel or a
portion thereof, determines the shape of the interior of the casting. Depending
also after it is drawn on the characteristics of the coating material and how it
is conveyed to the exhaust end of the mandrel, the interior of the mandrel may
have to contain jacketing or conduit means for moving a heat transfer fluid
therethru to prevent volatizing or burning said coating LW 9/8/63 JC - 8/16/63
THIS CONFIDENTIAL MATTER READ & UNDERSTOOD BY EW DATE 9/17/63

### Page 132
(coat outside) Material. The continuous casting die or mold may also have to be
water cooled (if casting or extruding steel or other metal which will otherwise
be at a temperature so high when it passes the end of the mandrel or extension
thereof thru which coating material is introduced as to prevent desired coating
from forming. In other words, the temperature of the casting is so controlled by
heat transfer to the die or mold and casting itself (air or liquid blown there
against) so that, when the coating material (plastic, chromate, or any other) is
applied thereto, the surface to which it is applied will be at the correct
temperature for best results. If thermoplastic plastic is sprayed from the
mandrel or extension as a powder, solution or molten spray against the inside
surface of the  pipe as it extrudes or is formed to shape as in casting, the
temperature of the surface receiving said plastic is preferably  just above the
melting point of the plastic (300 degrees F to 500 degrees F for most plastics).
The coating material may also be extrusion coated onto the inside surface of the
pipe from the mandrel. It may also comprise ceramic or metal sprayed onto the
inside surface of the moving casting as a molten liquid or powder. Powdered
aluminum, for example, may be introduced thru the mandrel and applied as a spray

Enterprises, College Point (Saales Manager) he informed us that his company was

about my conceived machine arrangements as follows. (a) Extrusion of sheet
plastic and immediate feeding to split vacuum forming die. THIS CONFIDENTIAL

of toluene to cause polymerization of polyethylene directly on the surface.

catalyst thru and pass a gas thru porous media. Ethylene gas causes immediate
polymerization of polyethylene. (c) Toluene and catalyst may be sloshed in a
hollow mold and ~~ g ~~ ethylene gas admitted thereto ~~ and ~~ under sufficient
pressure to cause polymerization of polyethylene as a shell on the inside of the
mold. Gas is not bubbled thru the toluene. EW 9/17/63

Method of Molding A method of molding decorated articles is conceived in which a
sheet or film of decorated plastic (or metal) is pressure drawn into a cavity in
a mold or forced therein to conform to the shape of the cavity wall after which
(when the film is retained in position) molding material is injected or
otherwise admitted to the cavity of the mold and molded against the pressure
formed film or sheet (thermoformed or otherwise) to become integral therewith
during the molding process by fusing therewith or physically interlocking with
portions of the sheet so formed. Globe Structure A world globe is conceived
consisting of two shells each of which comprises a sphere assembled of
respective half shells, one inside the other. The inner shell is made of thin
vacuum formed plastic sheet with countries of the world printed on its outer
surface. The outer spherical shells is injection molded of two pieces and its
inside diameter is approximately the outside diameter of the inside shell.
Molded flanges of the outer shell halves snap together and retain flanges or
flange portions of the inner shell at the same time. 10-10-63 VM EJW 10/24/63

### Page 212

frequently desired to decorate, color or otherwise affect the surface of the
article to impart special characteristics thereto, not preordered by the
material molded. To effect such surface treatment, the article is usually
removed from the mold and thereafter prepositioned relative to means for
rolling, spraying or otherwise applying a decoration or secondary material to
the surface. The procedure is relatively costly since it requires rehandling the
article and frequently the need to preposition the article by manual or
automatic means on fixtures, conveyors or the like. Accordingly, a primary
object of this invention is to provide a new and improved method for decorating
molded articles of manufacture while they are being molded so as to eliminate
the need ~~ and~~ to further handle and post decorate said articles. ~~ and

of open end of container) J Lemelson Method of Molding or Forging It is
conceived to mold a material such as metal to shape in a mold from liquid,
powder or solid semi-molten state and , at some time after it solidifies or
begins to solidity, causing the walls of the mold to compress the molded
material by one or more of several techniques. (a) In a first technique, the
mold is made of paramagnetic material such as steel and is caused to 11-14-63 VM

### Page 235

Magnetically reduce mold wall cavity and/ or molded metal to squeeze & improve
its qualities also ex. & collapse extrusion die, etc compress or inwardly deform
against the molded (or extruded) piece while still in the mold ( or extrusion
die) by generating an intense magnetic field around the mold of a characteristic
to cause inward deformation of the mold wall. (b) In a second technique, a band,
frame or portion of the mold is made of paramagnetic material and is
magnetically deformed (below the elastic limit thereof) to react against the
mold wall and inwardly deform it against the molded piece. (c) In a third
technique, the molded part itself is caused to expand and/or contract by
generating an intense magnetic field in or around the mold (or die) to cause
working of the molded or extruded piece. (d) In a fourth technique, a large
force is applied with an actuator to the wall of the mold or die (either as a
constant/and/or intermittent force) to cause it to compress the molded piece or
extrusion prior to its removal therefrom No permanent deformation occurs. (e) In
a fifth technique, a piece inserted into or molded integral with the molded part
is caused to magnetically expand/and/or contract to compress and works the
molding or forging against the mold wall. 11-14-63 VM

Blow Mold Decor. – Por plug Decoration of Blow Molded Items It is conceived to
decorate articles as they are blow molded (or possibly vacuum drawn items or
items which are formed by pressure forcing a sheet of plastic) as follows: (a)
Provide a portion of the wall of the mold adjacent those portions of the piece
to be molded made of a porous material such as porous sintered metal (stainless
steel, ceramic or other material which is porous). (2) Feed printing material
such as ink, lacquer or other colorant for the surface of the item to be
decorated through the porous portions by one of two methods (a) either under
constant low pressure feed or (b) program control the feed (or pressurization of
the decorating material to be pulsed just as the plastic parison or sheet is
blown thereagainst) to cause a quantity of said material to be imprinted on the
areas of the blown article aligned with the porous wall portions and to for
decorations or illustrations thereon; apply suction if necessary to the porous
member thereafter to prevent exusion or spillage of the decorating material. If
necessary, heat the porous portions continuously.

VM 11-14-63 LW 11/22/63

### Page 244
or program control the heating thereof to occur intermittently at time intervals
to maintain flow or at predetermined intervals in a cycle to present material
such as thermoplastic material in a semi-molten state as it flows against the
surface of the work II If the technique is applied to decorate pressure formed
or vacuum formed articles vacuum may be applied by program control of a valve or
pump(vacuum) to ~~preven~~ the porous members from beyond the wall of the mold
to prevent the vacuum applied to the molding cavity from drawing the decorating
liquid into the cavity or its wall. The vacuum may be applied for just that
interval that vacuum is applied to the mold cavity to draw the plastic sheet
therein and pressure may be applied under the control of the same programmer to
the porous portion of the wall (may be porous or it may be a series of small
holes) to force the decorating material into contact with the surface of the
article against the molded article at the proper instant. VM 11-14-63 LW
11/22/63

### Page 245
Process A (1) Extrude and calender a first sheet of plastic continuously. (2)
Cool and solidify as it is guided away from the extruder. (3) Continuously roll
print on at least one surface of the freshly formed and solidified sheet. (4)
Reheat the decorated sheet as it travels by radiation means and/or contact with
the printing rolls. (5) Continuously vacuum and/or pressure form the sheet into
mold cavities registered with the decoration. (6) Continuously die-cut into
articles registered with printing and formation. Process B Repeat steps 1–4 for
two sheets and thereafter: (5) Clampingly engage predetermined portions of both
sheets together between portions of a split mold and blow the engaged envelope
into the cavities of the mold while welding them together where no clamping is
provided.

### Page 246
essentially a blow molded article which is surface decorated when molded. (6)
Automatically trim or die cut the formation or blow preferably with the same
means used to weld them together (i.e. use a welding die with a cutting edge
adjacent thereto and contoured to the shape of the article so produced). (7)
Automatically handle or convey the article from the mold to prevent damage to
decorating. J. Lemelson Material from p 148 to this point witnessed & understood

the O'Hare Airport I met Jim Du Pont of Thermoplastic Processes, Stirling, NJ. I
discussed various topics relating to plastic processing with him. He suggested I
come out to his plant to 11-21-63 VM LW 12/2/63 THIS CONFIDENTIAL MATTER READ &

see him and offered to pay a royalty if I present him with new ideas which he
can produce. One of the products I questioned him about as to feasability is the
concept of applying one colored plastic as a thin strip or strips to extruded or
blown plastic (of another color) film in order to decorate same or to reinforce
same. He said it could be done and I expressed the opinion that there would be a
substantial market for such a product. I also suggested that perhaps the
striping device or extruder could be operated in the manner as taught in my
patent to limit the length of decorative strips by programmed stoppage and
restart of flow of the decorative material. It is also conceived by me to
provide a net-like decoration on film by oscillating or rotating portions of the
extrusion die thru which the decorating meterial is flowing to form a

of the article defined inside of the opening(s) in the mask. It is also
conceived to automatically control the amount and size of the particles or
droplets so sprayed by electro-optical scanning means generating a feedback
signal which is analyzed Jerome Lemelson 12/10/63 LW 12-11-63 VM 12-11-63

The benefits to be derived from charging the mask the same polarity as the

It is also conceived to program control the charge of the mask and/or particles

Methods of Coating Pipe Process A I.Comprising the step of 1. Heat pipe or small
portion thereof (progressive ~~ surf ~~ heating of inside surface) above melting
point of molybdenum or other primer metal ~~ and pour 2. Flow liquid primer
metal (such as molybdenum) thru pipe/pump or gravity) & coat surface with same
or 2' vacuum deposite or plate primer metal thereon as a coating then 3. Flow
thru liquid aluminum in liquid or powder state to provide a uniform coating
while temp of pipe is above that of aluminum. 4. Plastic particles may next be
flowed thru pipe while above their melting point but not so high as to burn
plastic to coat pipe Process B C 1. Continuously cast and draw or extrude metal
pipe and introduce one or more metals and/or plastics thru casting or extrusion
mandrel to coat interior of some while at the necessary temperature.

Dec. 23,63A zone refining technique for purifying metals involves the procedure
of melting a quantity of metal with an electron beam or beam of intense laser
generated light and removing or moving the impurities by one or more of several
techniques including (a) scanning the melt by electro-optical means including an
intense light beam or electron beam which is deflection controlled THIS
CONFIDENTIAL MATTER READ & UNDERSTOOD BY E Waldmeyer DATE 1/14/64 12-30-63 VM

### Page 278
an is operative to generated changes in a photo-electric or infra-red detector
which occur when impurities occur in the melt (or in a sheet or other shape).

variation such unpurities, can  electron or light he is automatically employed
thereafter to either (a) vaporize and remove the impurity , (b) move the
impurity along the melt, (c) a combination of (a) + (b), movement of the
impurity and/or that part of the melt containing the impurity maybe effected by
an electromagnetic field generated in and adjacent the melt and moved or
switched so as to move the melt. J. Karlin Improvements in the Continuous

magnetic forces applied to one or more of (a) the billet itself, (b) a ram or
other device operating on the billet and/or (c) the extrusion die, mold or
extrusion chamber. It is known that as intense magnetic filed suddenly applied
to ferromagnetic material will cause the material to deform  who such as reduce
in volume or change shape until the field is released. Such a field may be
applied to a billet found extruded to reduce its length and during said
application of magnetic force and reduction in length, a device similar to a
piston or extrusion ram may be advanced and retained against the rear face of
the billet whereupon when the magnetic field is removed the reaction of the
billet in expanding against the piston is operative to force the billet through
the extrusion die. The process may be accomplished by repeating such cycle many
times to complete the extrusion of the billet in which movement of the ram or
piston is synchronized to the application of the magnetic field so as to coact
therewith in effecting extrusion. Simultaneously with applicatoin of a magnetic
field to cause reduction in the length of the THIS CONFIDENTIAL MATTER READ &

1963 ILLUMINATED HIGHWAY MARKER

JAN 8-

I picked up a model of my illuminated highway marker (light and battery housing
secured to the top of a flexible delineator highway cone per my patent entitled
same) from United Telecontrol Corp of Farmingdale, New Jersey. Certain
modifications made and conceived therefore which will be presented to Radiator
Specialty Company of Charlotte, N.C. when their sales manager comes to New York
in the next week or so. (I called Mr. Alexanderson of Radiator today). I. Ref.

portion 12 defining the side wall (machined of aluminum) and capped with an
upper end wall 14 and a lower end wall 13 which threadably assemble therewith
end are moved with spanner wrenches. The side-wall 12 has substantially the same

a surface to be machined of sufficient intensity to heat that portion of the

the material. 2. Method in accordance with claim 1 in which said stream of fluid
is an overt gas. 3. Method in accordance with claim 1 in which said stream of

CONFIDENTIAL MATTER READ & UNDERSTOOD BY DEVICES & METHODS for administering
Skin Adsorbtion Chemicals to the Human Body. Reference is made to the recently
announced chemical BLH, a derivative of lignum, which when placed on the skin of
a human, disappears thru the pores into the skin and is shortly thereafter
absorbed into the bloodstream. Several devices for administering this chemical
and chemicals carried thereby into the human body are conceived, viz. I: A
device is conceived which ~~stro ~~ is strapped, taped or otherwise secured to
the human body and which automatically releases either continuously or
intermittently, predetermined amounts of adsorbtion chemican to the

Tool smoothes out- weld by beam - oscillating, rotating, spreader tool Beam &
Tool

FIG. 1 surface of the skin which adsorbs said released amounts for performing
the desired medicinal, nourishment, anaesthetic or other function. Release of
the chemical from a small container thereof in the strappedon device, may be
effected by gravity, capillary action, movement of the body, heat of the body
pressurizing a container for the liquid, or a mechanical spring operated
timerrelease mechanism (such as a watch-type mechanism operating a valve to open
and close and either compressed gas or spring operated pressurization of the
liquid container) or a battery operated timer and pressurizing means such as a

Strain Gage Construction A new type of strain gage thermocouple is conceived
consisting of a vacuum deposited or electron beam deposited sensing element
bonded to a layer of oxidized metal or oxide material provided on a strip,
filament or other wire shaped metal which strip, etc. is welded or bonded to the
test specimen. Fabrication technique include. I. (a) Provide a base strip of
metal such as stainless steel, titanium, zirconium or any suitable alloy. ~~
Deposite ~~ Either deposite a layer of metal on a surface of said strip and
oxidize the surface thereof or the entire layer, or oxidize a strata of the
surface of the strip or vacuum deposite an insulating oxidizing material onto
the surface of the strip. (b) Next selectively deposit strain gage or
thermocouple sensing element onto the upper surface of the oxide or insulating
material to the desired shape. This may be done by beam thru a mask, by beam or
heat etching thru a mask placed over a deposited layer of said sensing or

Violet Mitchell 1-23-64

### Page 12
Beam etch Beam oxidizing strain gage material, by selective beam deposition. (c)
Provide lead attachments to ends of sensing element or complete a microminiature
circuit therewith by vacuum and beam deposition means which circuit includes
amplifying and short wave transmission means to transmit signals from the strain
gage on thermocouple element as it operates. A battery may also be deposited for
powering the circuit or induction coupling means to generate electrical energy
for powering said circuit when subjected to a changing magnetic field or a
thermoelectric generating element or elements may be vacuum deposited or
attached to the circuit as deposited for powering same. * (d) Next step is to
vacuum deposite or otherwise apply an insulating coating over the sending
element. This may be accomplished by techniques such as

Plate - meth of making circuits oxidize to provide any shape described, namely
either depositing an insulating material such as magnesium, oxide, al oxide,
titanium oxide, or fluorides of metals such as these or by depositing a layer of
metal and completely converting same to an oxide, fluoride, etc or by converting
the exposed surface of the sensing element to an oxide by exposure, for example,
to Hydrogen fluoride gas, etc. Plating and heat or beam etching technique may be
applied to the above procedures. Also signal generated by strain gage or
thermocouple may be capacitatively inductively transferred to another circuit by
providing a deposited inductor in circuit with the strain or thermocouple
element as disclosed in a previous notebook of mine.

This invention relates to constructions in novelties and the like - and in
particular, to ~~ an ~~ a ~~ novell ~~ mock figurine adopted for ~~ rent ~~
retentive assembly with the rim of a bowl or glass. It is a primary object of
this invention to provide a structure in a novelty so shaped to permit it to be
easily secured to and removed from the rim of a drinking cup, glass or bowl.
Another object is to provide a retaining device for a drinking straw which may
easily secured to a drinking cup or glass and will permit prepositioning said
straw to facilitate its use by a small child. Another object is to provide a
device molded in a single operation and may be ~~novelty which may be ~~ having
plurality of appendages and so shaped as to be frictionally retainable against
the rim of a glass, cup or bowl without falling off when the glass or cup is
tilted. Another object is to provide a one piece plastic toy figure, easily
assembleable

visited yesterday a I left drawings and prints with him as follows (a) Miss
America and Miss Universe Dolls (b) Male occupation dolls (miner, policeman,
sportsman, executive, surgeon, and ~~ appro ~~ a description of approximately 40
different occupational dolls with molded plastic accesories in which I proposed
packing of each in shrink film open boxes with their accessories. ~~ Sam ~~ I
visited Sam Freimauer and Joe Lieberman of Frey-Lieb Company at 487 Broadway
with Jules Cotler yesterday and offered to analyze their new crank record player
and propose improvements therein which, they agreed, if adapted by

them and incorporated into their record player they would pay me a 3% royalty on
the selling price of the record player. One such improvement proposed by me in
Jules Cotler's presence was a structure in the housing to facilitate mounting in
a toy as illustrated below a

full length wall lugs to support long screws to hold housing in toy - Tubular

construction was conceived and sketched for Joe Lieberman and Sam Freimauer in
my presence on June 23, 1964 Jules Cotler 1/24/64 Lenore Waldmeyer 1/29/64

Fabrication of speaker unit itself. Frey's current speaker is pressed fiber

Game - rec. play. the entire speaker (diaphragm, supporting frame, lug mounts
and center vibrator coupling) of a quality plastic such as impact styrene,
urethane polymer (Seclon), Celcon, ABS, etc plastic) or to form same from thin
sheet by known or modified thermoforming techniques. These structures, methods
and apparatus for producing an audio speaker may be patentable and I intend to
file patent applications, if so: (A) Thermoformed speaker and/or diaphragm
therefore. Since the diaphragm is relatively thin and its support or frame
heavier, it is conceived to thermoform a sheet of thermoplastic ( into a cavity
in a mold the shape of the diaphragm while restraining the sheet material
adjacent the cavity from flowing therein. Thus the central portion of the sheet
which flows into the cavity will thin out but the rim of the speaker diaphragm
remains the same thickness JC - 1/24/64 THIS CONFIDENTIAL MATTER READ AND
UNDERSTOOD BY LW DATE 1/29/64

The following games and toys using a record player of the type disclosed on
pages 30 to this point are conceived and will be presented to Transogram Ive,
Pressman Toy Corp, Hassenfeld Bros, etc in confidence with the understanding
that a royalty will be paid for their use. I. Games of chance and/or skill where
random playback of recordings on the record played wherein the record player
housing is molded integral with the playing board, attached thereto or part of a
separate playing unit and the random playback of recordings or records results
in word instructions for the game (i.e. - the player cranks the record player
and the word, phrase, or sentence played back (randomly)dictates a move on the
playing board). II Wheeled toys wherein the crank for the record played is
coupled to be. 2-3-64 VM This confidential matter read and understood by LW
Date  1/29/24 JC 1/24/64 driven by the shaft (or a shaft coupled thereto by
gears) of the wheels rotated as the toy is pulled, pushed or powered. In this
respect, the push-button projecting from the housing which operates to lift the
spring loaded speaker off the tone arm to permit spring return of the arm to the
edge of the record may be activated by a cam or cam activated link to lift said
speaker assembly automatically to play the next recording. The same principle
may be applied to a gear motor driving the crank mechanism, the shift of which
motor or one geared to its shaft is coupled or connected to the present record
turning crank shaft ~~ end ~~ and a crank or cam thereon or associated with and
driven by said motor shaft is operative to periodically effect lifting of the ~~
mc ~~ speaker away from the tone arm to permit return of the latter to the edge
of the record for replay. 2-3-64 VM JC 1/24/64  This confidential matter read &

III Toys and game devices in which the crank shaft 19 (Fig.1 p36) either has a
gear (pulley or cam) secured thereto or an extension thereof which is coupled to
a further mechanism in the toy for creating a viewable mechanical action (or
closing an electrical switch) as the crank or shaft is turned to provide action
plus sound. Said shaft 17 maybe pinned, geared, pulley mounted, etc. to create,
for example, (a) movement of the mouth of a doll as the record playing is
transduced to sound (b) rotation of a disc past a window in a housing to present
different pictures,(c)movent of a belt containing pictures, (d) movement of
magnets under a surface to move paramagnetic objects on the surface, or most any
suitable action, (e) Talking figure toys (stuffed, blow or injection molded,

    Saturday Jan 25, 1964 Mr Reyer Swan, Jules Cotler and myself visited Mr Jim
    Du Pont of Thermoplastic Equipment Corp. to discuss equipment for extrusion

Plasma refinery 101 a melt of the metal to be refined and feeding same to a
plasma arc (or feeding shapes such as powder, rod, wire, etc of the metal to the
refined to a plasma arc) and vaporizing the metal in the plasma arc. Then, by
applying an electrode or electrodes adjacent the arc which are charged to the
right potential and/or magnetic fields generated in the vicinity of the arc,
cause the ionized atoms of the metal to be attracted to a plate, wire, sheet or
other shape which is preferably in motion or movable automatically to permit
metal deposited thereon to be removed therefrom. The base plate sheet, or other
shape may be automatically conveyed past the plasma arc in an atmosphere (or
vacuum past metal vapor so formed) and may comprise the same material being
purified or refined or a material to be alloyed therewith if it is to be 2-25-64

Theft Identification by electronics It is conceived to provide a simple
macro-electronic or semi-conductor integrated ~~chi ~~ electronic device capable
of emitting a binary digital code or particular frequency signal whenever its
input is pulsed with a current and to use said device attached to an article or
vehicle which may be pilfered, in such a manner as to identify the vehicle when
it comes within range of a receiver which is programmed to indicate by
energizing an alarm or other means that the code generator is within range. To
reduce the probability of theft of motor vehicles or indicate other indicate
when a vehicle is ~~ in ~~ which has been reported stolen is within range of a
monitor, the following concepts are conceived by me and will be developed as
part of a patent application. (a) ~~A ~~ Micro-electronic, integrated circuits
are provided together with self contained (or other) means for

### Page 84
energizing 3-11-64 V.M. THIS CONFIDENTIAL MATTER READ & UNDERSTOOD BY EJW DATE

### Page 85
same to generate a particular binary digital code or frequency signal for each
unit and units are secured to respective motor vehicles. In other words, each
motor vehicle is provided with a code or tone generator of the short wave type
which will generate a different code or tone identifying signal than all other
code or tone generators in use. The ~~code~~identifying signal(s) may be
generated periodically at all times (during the life of the battery which may be
years) or while the engine is running. (b) The identifying signal generator is
preferably located where it cannot easily be silenced or pampered with. A good
location may be in a housing containing a part vital to the operation of the
vehicle such that removal of the housing, part or device will prevent operation
of the vehicle or will not be easily accomplished. Placement of THIS

### Page 94
and control as well as extinguish fires of various types. A system is conceived
having the following components and operational characteristics. I. Sensors - A
plurality of stationery fire sensing devices of the same or different
operational characteristics such as infra-red detectors, (cells), optical
detectors, bi-metallic relays, etc are provided throughout an area, building,
yard, countryside, etc to be protected each operative to generate a signal or
signals in response to radiation generated by a fire, heat, smoke, etc and each
coupled to means for generating a specific code or tone signal and transmitting
same by short wave (radio or microwave or wires) to a control computer upon
detecting a fire, smoke, etc (Could be used in a forrest for fire control.). One
or more of the sensors (called monitor sensor stations hereafter) may have
associated therewith 3-11-64 VM THIS CONFIDENTIAL MATTER READ & UNDERSTOOD

models pp. 118, 119 electronic means for determining (a) degree of temperature,
(b) area covered by fire, etc and for transmitting codes and/or tone signals

sensor stations may also have or comprise a television camera thereat
automatically operative to ~~ be ~~ have its scanning optical system turn
directed at the fire and, in certain instances, focused or otherwise adjusted
automatically and/or under remote control by the short wave transmission of
command control codes from the computer and/or an operator stationed at a video
receiver console. II ~~ The s ~~ Supplemental Sensors may be used to aid in
fighting the fire. These may comprise one or more mobile scanning devices of the

equipment. 3-11-64 VM THIS CONFIDENTIAL MATTER READ & UNDERSTOOD BY EJW DATE

### Page 95
The mobile units may be positioned at strategic locations on the ground by fire

otherwise attached etc. They may also be dropped from a helicopter, aircraft, or
rocket by parachute or other means. III. The fire control computer may is
